- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms

- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Kafka ACL Authorization Code Audit

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in `apache/kafka` that implement or define Access Control List (ACL) authorization logic. Search under `core/src/main/` and `clients/src/main/` for files containing classes or interfaces with `Authorizer` or `AclAuthorizer` in the name. For each file, report the class name and whether it defines the interface, implements it, or provides test utilities.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)


Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive audit of the Apache Kafka repository for ACL authorization logic. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I identified **17 Java source files** across three main modules that implement ACL authorization in Apache Kafka:

### Key Interfaces (Defining Contracts):
1. **`Authorizer`** - The core pluggable interface for Kafka authorization
2. **`ClusterMetadataAuthorizer`** - Extends Authorizer for KRaft-based ACL storage
3. **`AuthorizerServerInfo`** - Runtime broker metadata interface
4. **`AuthorizableRequestContext`** - Request context interface
5. **`AclMutator`** - Controller interface for ACL mutations

### Main Implementation:
- **`StandardAuthorizer`** - The built-in ACL implementation that stores ACLs in the cluster metadata log

### Supporting Classes:
- Data models: `StandardAcl`, `StandardAclWithId`, `StandardAuthorizerData`, `AclCache`
- Result classes: `AclCreateResult`, `AclDeleteResult`
- Utilities: `AclEntry`, `AuthorizerUtils`, `Action`, `AuthorizationResult`

The files span three key directories:
- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/authorizer/` - Interface definitions
- `metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/authorizer/` - Implementation and data handling
- `server/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/security/authorizer/` - Utilities

The results have been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed categorization of each file's role in the authorization framework.

Authorizer implementation starts loading its metadata.</li>\\n51:  *   <li>Broker starts SocketServer to accept connections and process requests.</li>\\n52:  *   <li>For each listener, SocketServer waits for authorization metadata to be available in the\\n53:  *       authorizer before accepting connections. The future returned by {@link #start(AuthorizerServerInfo)}\\n54:  *       for each listener must return only when authorizer is ready to authorize requests on the listener.</li>\\n55:  *   <li>Broker accepts connections. For each connection, broker performs authentication and then accepts Kafka requests.\\n56:  *       For each request, broker invokes {@link #authorize(AuthorizableRequestContext, List)} to authorize\\n57:  *       actions performed by the request.</li>\\n58:  * </ol>\\n59:  *\\n60:  * Authorizer implementation class may optionally implement @{@link org.apache.kafka.common.Reconfigurable}\\n61:  * to enable dynamic reconfiguration without restarting the broker.\\n62:  * <p>Authorizer implementation class may also optionally implement {@link org.apache.kafka.common.metrics.Monitorable}\\n63:  * to enable the authorizer to register metrics. The following tags are automatically added to all metrics registered:\\n64:  * <code>config</code> set to <code>authorizer.class.name</code>, <code>class</code> set to the Authorizer class name,\\n65:  * and <code>role</code> set to either <code>broker</code> or <code>controller</code>.\\n66:  * <p>\\n67:  * <b>Threading model:</b>\\n68:  * <ul>\\n69:  *   <li>All authorizer operations including authorization and ACL updates must be thread-safe.</li>\\n70:  *   <li>ACL update methods are asynchronous. Implementations with low update latency may return a\\n71:  *       completed future using {@link java.util.concurrent.CompletableFuture#completedFuture(Object)}.\\n72:  *       This ensures that the request will be handled synchronously by the caller without using a\\n73:  *       purgatory to wait for the result. If ACL updates require remote communication which may block,\\n74:  *       return a future that is completed asynchronously when the remote operation completes. This enables\\n75:  *       the caller to process other requests on the request threads without blocking.</li>\\n76:  *   <li>Any threads or thread pools used for processing remote operations asynchronously can be started during\\n77:  *       {@link #start(AuthorizerServerInfo)}. These threads must be shutdown during {@link Authorizer#close()}.</li>\\n78:  * </ul>\\n79:  * </p>\\n80:  */\\n81: public interface Authorizer extends Configurable, Closeable {\\n82: \\n83:     /**\\n84:      * Starts loading authorization metadata and returns futures that can be used to wait until\\n85:      * metadata for authorizing requests on each listener is available. Each listener will be\\n86:      * started only after its metadata is available and authorizer is ready to start authorizing\\n87:      * requests on that listener.\\n88:      *\\n89:      * @param serverInfo Metadata for the broker including broker id and listener endpoints\\n90:      * @return CompletionStage for each endpoint that completes when authorizer is ready to\\n91:      *         start authorizing requests on that listener.\\n92:      */\\n93:     Map<Endpoint, ? extends CompletionStage<Void>> start(AuthorizerServerInfo serverInfo);\\n94: \\n95:     /**\\n96:      * Authorizes the specified action. Additional metadata for the action is specified\\n97:      * in `requestContext`.\\n98:      * <p>\\n99:      * This is a synchronous API designed for use with locally cached ACLs. Since this method is invoked on the\\n100:      * request thread while processing each request, implementations of this method should avoid time-consuming\\n101:      * remote communication that may block request threads.\\n102:      *\\n103:      * @param requestContext Request context including request type, security protocol and listener name\\n104:      * @param actions Actions being authorized including resource and operation for each action\\n105:      * @return List of authorization results for each action in the same order as the provided actions\\n106:      */\\n107:     List<AuthorizationResult> authorize(AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext, List<Action> actions);\\n108: \\n109:     /**\\n110:      * Creates new ACL bindings.\\n111:      * <p>\\n112:      * This is an asynchronous API that enables the caller to avoid blocking during the update.
